### [p003_c0001] 1. THE BRONX BUS NETWORK: REDESIGNED

## Page 4

### [p004_c0001] THE BRONX BUS NETWORK: REDESIGNED
[p004_c0002] The Bronx Bus Network Redesign is New York City Transit’s first borough-wide bus network redesign conducted as part of the Fast Forward Plan initiative to Reimagine the Bus Network . Over the past year, we gathered all available bus service data and analyzed demographics for the Bronx. We also engaged extensively with elected officials, community boards, and communities throughout the borough and in Manhattan where certain Bronx routes operate. The Final Plan draws on this work, and the findings presented in the Existing Conditions and Draft Plan reports. 1
[p004_c0003] The redesigned network outlined in the following pages establishes a strong foundation on which we can continue to build a successful high-frequency network that serves the largest number of riders at the times when they need service the most. While this report details changes being made to the routes, frequencies, and spans of service that make up the Bronx Bus Network, it also demonstrates our new approach to providing bus service—one that dynamically responds and adapts to the needs and travel patterns of customers and reallocates available resources where they will have the greatest impact. Therefore, our work on the Bronx Bus Network does not end with the release of this report or the implementation of the proposed changes, but will continue as we refine service based on ridership and performance, and respond to feedback we receive from customers.
> [p004_c0004] graph LR; A["Market and Service Data Analyses and Public Outreach"] --> B["Redraw Network and Develop Draft Plan"]; B --> C["Public Input and Final Plan development"]; C --> D(["Final Plan Public Outreach"]); A --- A1["• Publish Existing Conditions Report February 2019"]; B --- B1["• Publish Draft Plan May 2019"]; C --- C1["• Publish Final Plan October 2019"] The diagram illustrates the Bronx Bus Network Redesign process as a sequential flow. It begins with a box labeled "Market and Service Data Analyses and Public Outreach". An arrow points from this box to a second box labeled "Redraw Network and Develop Draft Plan". From the second box, an arrow points to a third box labeled "Public Input and Final Plan development". Finally, an arrow points from the third box to an oval labeled "Final Plan Public Outreach". To the right of each of the first three boxes, there is a bullet point indicating a publication date: "• Publish Existing Conditions Report February 2019" next to the first box, "• Publish Draft Plan May 2019" next to the second box, and "• Publish Final Plan October 2019" next to the third box.
[p004_c0005] _1 This document is intended to support and—to an extent—finalize the findings and proposed improvements presented in the previous documents, with revisions. To learn more about the background research grounding the Final Plan, as well as a wealth of data and route-by-route bus service summaries, see the Existing Conditions Report. To learn more about the Network Redesign process and to see how our proposals have progressed since Spring 2019, see the Draft Plan._
[p004_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 4_

## Page 5

### [p005_c0001] Network Redesign Goals
[p005_c0002] “Reimagining our bus network means customer focused routes, faster and more reliable travel times, and comfortable and environmentally sustainable buses.”
### [p005_c0003] – Fast Forward Plan
[p005_c0004] We used the following tactics in our redesign of the Bronx Bus Network to improve travel times and bus reliability for bus customers in the borough:
- [p005_c0005] • Increased frequency of buses by building an all-day frequent network • Created more direct routings • Balanced bus stop spacing • Enhanced connectivity • Expanded bus priority
[p005_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 5_

## Page 6

### [p006_c0001] All-day Frequent Network
[p006_c0002] In the redesigned Bronx Bus Network, we identified key corridors to serve as the foundation for a network of sustainable, all-day bus service that is reliable and moves riders as quickly as possible. 2 Presently, many bus corridors have frequent service during the AM (7:00am-9:00am) and PM (4:00pm-7:00pm) peak periods. However, this frequency tapers off during the midday and evening “off-peak” periods. Customers still need to get around quickly and reliably during off-peak hours. So, we bolstered frequency during these off-peak periods to provide frequent service consistently throughout the day.
> [p006_c0003] The map displays the Bronx Bus Network with various bus routes color-coded by their all-day frequency. A legend in the top right corner, titled 'All-Day Frequency*', defines the color coding: dark red for '8-minutes or better', light red for '15-minutes or better', and yellow for '30-minutes or better'. Grey lines represent 'Peak-only service'. The map shows a dense network of routes, with the highest frequency (8-minutes or better) concentrated in the central and western parts of the Bronx. Surrounding areas like Yonkers, New Rochelle, and Pelham Manor are also labeled. The Hudson River is to the west, the East River to the south, and Long Island Sound to the east. A scale bar and north arrow are located at the bottom center.
[p006_c0004] _2 All-day bus service is defined as bus service that operates consistently throughout the day and into the evening. From 7:00am to 9:00pm._
[p006_c0005] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 6_

## Page 11

### [p011_c0001] Bus Stop Balancing
[p011_c0002] Stop removals and adjustments— together known as bus stop balancing — are especially important to achieve our goals of speeding up buses and increasing reliability. Currently, New York City has the shortest distances between its bus stops of any major city, with an average of 805 feet between stops*. In the Bronx, that average is slightly higher, at 882 feet. Both are shorter than the distance between stops in international peer transit systems around the world, which typically ranges from 1,000 to 1,680 feet. While it may be super convenient to have a bus stop right outside your door, too many bus stops too close together dramatically slow down the bus and worsen reliability. Each time the bus stops, it must exit traffic, load and unload passengers, and wait to reenter traffic, resulting in decreased speed and increased travel times. The waiting time for a bus to re-enter traffic can range from 20 seconds during off-peak travels times to more than one minute during peak rush hour. By removing closely-spaced and underutilized stops, we can keep buses moving with the flow of traffic and get riders where they need to go more quickly.
[p011_c0003] Bus stop balancing involves an in-depth analysis of bus stop usage, analysis of the demographics of users—including those who would be most impacted by a stop removal, outreach to riders ( detailed in Appendix 2 ), and potential improvements to remaining bus stops. The average distance between stops in the Bronx is 1,092 feet in our Final Plan, bringing it in line with international standards.
[p011_c0004] *Note: this reflects average stop spacing for regular bus service (local, limited, and SBS) routes.
### [p011_c0005] Speeding up the Bus
[p011_c0006] Farther from the bus stop, faster buses
> [p011_c0007] The diagram shows a vertical purple line representing a bus route on a grid of white streets. Four purple bus icons are positioned along the route at regular intervals. At the bottom left, a blue house icon and a green walking person icon are shown. A yellow dashed line connects the house to the bus stop, with the text '5 Min' written next to it, indicating the travel time from the residential area to the bus stop.
### [p011_c0008] Close-Stop Spacing
[p011_c0009] Closer to the bus stop, slower buses
> [p011_c0010] The diagram shows a vertical orange line representing a bus route on a grid of white streets. Four orange bus icons are positioned along the route, with the first one very close to the bottom. At the bottom left, a blue house icon and a green walking person icon are shown. A yellow dashed line connects the house to the bus stop, with the text '2 Min' written next to it, indicating the travel time from the residential area to the bus stop.
[p011_c0011] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 11_

## Page 12

### [p012_c0001] Enhanced Connectivity
[p012_c0002] In the Existing Conditions Report, we mapped the Bronx's population and employment density to identify where customers need to go in 2019 and beyond. Our redesigned Bronx Bus Network directly improves connectivity in well-trafficked areas by enhancing service with new routing and increased frequency ( See Appendix 4 & 5 ). This increased frequency also makes transferring easier, expanding riders' access to destinations within the Bronx and in other boroughs. By increasing the frequency of service, we can reduce wait times for riders who are connecting to the bus route that will get them to their final destinations.
[p012_c0003] Transfers, then, are a crucial component of the Redesign process. Routes that work together to connect riders to their destinations are far more efficient than one meandering route that serves as a one-seat ride to the same destinations. Interconnected routes provide faster travel times and enable increased frequency. We recognize that the Redesign will result in some riders requiring an additional transfer to complete their trip. These passengers should not have to pay an additional fare to transfer. 3 The agency will seek to strategically add additional free transfers to the system.
### [p012_c0004] Central Bronx Jobs Reachable
> [p012_c0005] Average Weekday Trip (PM Peak) Proposed Route New access Existing access No Longer accessible Travel within 45 minutes by Bus from Central Bronx Data source: Google Maps 2018, NYEDC 2018 The map illustrates the Central Bronx's job reachability. A legend in the top left corner defines the symbols: a grey line for 'Proposed Route', a teal shaded area for 'New access', a light green shaded area for 'Existing access', and a grey shaded area for 'No Longer accessible'. The map itself is a detailed street map of the Central Bronx, with various landmarks and institutions labeled, including the Bronx Zoo, Fordham University, and the Bronx-Lebanon Hospital Center. A large teal area indicates 'New access' to jobs, while a light green area indicates 'Existing access'. A scale bar at the bottom right shows distances of 0, 0.6, and 1 mile, and a north arrow is also present.
[p012_c0006] _3 Our policy: No rider should have to pay an additional transfer fare as a result of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign._
[p012_c0007] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 12_

## Page 13

### [p013_c0001] Expanded Bus Priority
[p013_c0002] As part of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign planning process, MTA and NYCDOT conducted an analysis of major Bronx corridors to identify streets where bus lanes and other bus priority treatments would provide the biggest benefit to Bronx bus riders. The goal of this analysis was to use a variety of data sources to prioritize streets for further study, planning, design, and implementation of street treatments that enhance the customer benefits of our Bus Network Redesign. MTA and NYCDOT created corridor evaluation criteria based on the level of demand for bus service, bus speed and reliability, frequency of service in the proposed bus network, neighborhood demographics, and feasibility of implementing new street treatments. Each criterion was assigned a weight based on its relative significance. A total of 46 corridors were scored and ranked accordingly.
[p013_c0003] Below is the list of the highest-ranking corridors where bus priority improvements would most benefit Bronx bus riders. A detailed overview of each bus priority corridor can be found starting on page XX.
- [p013_c0004] • Pelham Parkway, Fordham Road, and West 207 Street (Eastchester Avenue to Broadway) • Pelham Bay Park 6 Station Area • Washington Bridge and West 181 Street (University Avenue to Broadway) • East 149 Street (River Avenue to Southern Boulevard) • E.L. Grant Highway (Cross Bronx Expressway to East 167 Street) • University Avenue (Kingsbridge Road to Cross Bronx Expressway) • Tremont Avenue (Sedgwick Avenue to Boston Road) • East 167 Street and East 168 Street (Jerome Avenue to Franklin Avenue) • Story Avenue (Bronx River Avenue to White Plains Road) • East Gun Hill Road (Bainbridge Avenue to Bartow Avenue)
[p013_c0005] NYCDOT will begin the planning process for these bus priority corridors with the release of this Plan. Outreach and implementation on the first set of corridors will start in 2020.
> [p013_c0006] A map of the Bronx, New York, highlighting the proposed bus priority corridors. The map shows a grid of streets with several major thoroughfares and bridges. The highlighted corridors are shown as thick blue lines. These include: West 207 St, University Ave, Fordham Rd, Pelham Parkway, Pelham Bay Park Station Area, Tremont Ave West, Tremont Ave East, East 167 St, East 168 St, Story Ave, East 149 St, East Gun Hill Rd, Washington Bridge, and 181 St. A north arrow is located in the bottom right corner.
[p013_c0007] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 13_

## Page 14

### [p014_c0001] Improved User Experience
[p014_c0002] With a redesigned bus network must come new bus maps. We're using the redesign as an opportunity to thoroughly examine how we communicate route and service information, with the goal of identifying types of service and frequency of service via our maps more clearly and intuitively. We're also exploring the creation of a bus map that shows overnight service.
### [p014_c0003] Real Time Bus Information
[p014_c0004] NYCDOT continues its initiative to bring real-time passenger information (RTPI) bus arrival data displays to bus stops. Since 2013, NYCDOT has installed 17 RTPI signs at non-SBS bus stops in the Bronx, all funded by the New York City Council. Over the next few years, additional RTPI signs will be installed in the Bronx through Resolution A (Reso A) City Council funding. Real-time bus information totems are also located in the Bronx along the Bx41, Bx6, and Q44 SBS routes. Customers can also use the MYmta app or visit mta.info for real time bus service information.
### [p014_c0005] Boarding the Bus and Payment
[p014_c0006] All-door boarding will be launched on all bus routes by 2021. This will significantly reduce the time required to board the bus, as well as alleviate some of the seemingly-overcrowded conditions that are caused by front-door boarding and passengers not moving toward the back of the bus. The new OMNY payment system, available on all buses and subways by the end of 2020, will allow customers to make tap-and-go fare payments with a smartphone or contactless credit or debit card, speeding up the payment process. Combined, these improvements should cut down on the amount of time spent boarding buses, which can be upcycled into more service for the same number of service hours, based on faster speeds along the route.
### [p014_c0007] OMNY:2021
[p014_c0008] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 14_

## Page 15

### [p015_c0001] 2. NETWORK-LEVEL IMPROVEMENTS

## Page 16

### [p016_c0001] NETWORK-LEVEL IMPROVEMENTS
### [p016_c0002] Regular Bus Service
[p016_c0003] The Bronx is comprised of many neighborhoods, each with its own unique transit service needs. For the Redesign, we evaluated each route and transit corridor through two lenses. First, we examined each route and corridor in its entirety to see how it serves the broader Bronx Bus Network. Second, we focused in at the neighborhood level to evaluate clusters of routes—sometimes only small portions of each route—to see how they work together to serve the Bronx's various neighborhoods. For example, the Bx42 serves a much different function for Morris Heights residents than it does for Throgs Neck residents, yet it is all one continuous route and its service must be configured as such. That said, by dividing the Bronx into separate service areas, we can understand each route's function throughout its many segments and determine the best course of action to improve service.
[p016_c0004] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 16_

## Page 22

### [p022_c0001] 3. BUS PRIORITY IMPROVEMENTS
- [p022_c0002] ◆ Potential Improvements to Study ◆ Bus Priority Corridors

## Page 23

### [p023_c0001] BUS PRIORITY IMPROVEMENTS
### [p023_c0002] Potential Improvements to Study
[p023_c0003] NYCDOT uses a variety of bus priority treatments to provide faster and more reliable bus service. For each bus priority corridor profiled beginning on page 26, NYCDOT will investigate improvements that may include the following:
### [p023_c0004] New Bus Lanes
> [p023_c0005] A photograph of a city street in New York City, likely the Bronx, showing a bus lane. On the left, a blue bus is stopped at a bus stop. A red-painted bus lane is marked with 'ONLY BUS' and 'ONLY' on the pavement. Yellow taxis and other vehicles are visible in the general traffic lanes. The street is lined with buildings and trees. A crosswalk is in the foreground. The NYC DOT logo is in the bottom right corner.
[p023_c0006] Bus lanes separate buses from general traffic, improving speed and reliability. They are typically located along the curb or “offset” from the curb, allowing the curb lane to be utilized for other purposes. Ensuring that bus lanes are not used by others is a challenge in New York City, so accompanying enforcement strategies are crucial for success. Automated Bus Lane Enforcement (ABLE) is now active on all M15 SBS buses, and will roll out on all M14 SBS and B44 SBS buses by November of 2019. The system, using cameras mounted on the front of buses, automatically captures photo and video evidence of vehicles blocking bus lanes. That visual evidence is then used to issue fines to offenders. Funding from the proposed 2020-2024 Capital Plan will be used to expand ABLE to additional routes throughout the City.
[p023_c0007] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 23_

## Page 24

### [p024_c0001] Upgraded Bus Lane
> [p024_c0002] A photograph of a city street intersection. The road surface is painted with red markings that say "ONLY BUS" in large, bold letters. Two buses are visible in the lane, and a yellow taxi is in the adjacent lane. Pedestrians are walking on the sidewalk. The image is credited to NYC DOT.
[p024_c0003] NYCDOT monitors all bus lanes and will upgrade bus lanes when warranted to make them more effective. This could include extending hours of bus lane enforcement, painting bus lanes red to clearly delineate them from normal travel lanes, changing curbside lanes to offset lanes, and other measures that improve the effectiveness of bus lanes and make the street work better for all users.
### [p024_c0004] Protected Bus Lane
> [p024_c0005] A photograph of a city street. A bus lane is marked with a red "ONLY BUS" sign on the pavement. A metal barrier is installed along the curb of the bus lane to prevent other vehicles from entering it. A bus is visible in the lane. The image is credited to NYC DOT.
[p024_c0006] Using barriers to protect a bus lane makes it more difficult for vehicles other than buses to illegally use the lane. This can improve the effectiveness of a bus lane where violations are rampant, but must be accompanied by measures that preserve essential access to the curb (e.g., emergency vehicles).
### [p024_c0007] Transit and Freight Priority Street
> [p024_c0008] A photograph of a city street. A bus is in the lane, and a truck is in the adjacent lane. The road surface is painted with red markings that say "ONLY BUS" and "ONLY TRUCK". The image is credited to NYC DOT.
[p024_c0009] A transit and freight priority street provides dedicated space for buses and trucks to traverse a corridor while limiting other through traffic. This type of treatment may include curb regulation changes and turn restrictions that help prioritize bus and truck movements along a corridor and reduce turns through crosswalks. A high-activity area with a mix of high bus volumes, truck traffic, and pedestrian activity may be a candidate for a transit and freight priority street.
### [p024_c0010] Bus Boarders
> [p024_c0011] A photograph of a city street. A bus is stopped at a bus stop, and a person is boarding the bus. The sidewalk is extended with a durable recycled plastic "bus boarder" that provides more space for waiting passengers. The image is credited to NYC DOT.
[p024_c0012] Bus bulbs are permanent sidewalk extensions at bus stops that provide more space for waiting passengers and allow buses to pull up to the curb without leaving the travel lane, saving valuable seconds. Recently, NYCDOT began using durable recycled plastic "bus boarders" that serve the same purpose but do not require capital construction.
### [p024_c0013] Bus Queue Jump Lane and Transit Signal Priority
> [p024_c0014] A photograph of a city street. A bus is in the lane, and a traffic signal is visible. The traffic signal is a "BUS QUEUE JUMP" signal, which allows a bus to enter an intersection before regular traffic and bypass waiting queues of traffic at a light, giving the bus a head start. The image is credited to NYC DOT.
[p024_c0015] In addition to corridor-wide transit signal priority (TSP) treatments, dedicated bus signal phases are another way to use traffic signals to give buses priority through an intersection. These bus queue jump signals allow a bus to enter an intersection before regular traffic and bypass waiting queues of traffic at a light, giving the bus a head start. Bus queue jump signals are often paired with bus lanes.
[p024_c0016] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 24_

## Page 25

### [p025_c0001] Curb Management
[p025_c0002] NYCDOT bus priority project planning includes an evaluation of curb regulations. Adequate and appropriate truck loading, passenger drop-off, and parking regulations can benefit bus operations by reducing double parking and the illegal use of bus lanes. Effective enforcement is also critical to ensure curb management success.
### [p025_c0003] Pedestrian Safety
[p025_c0004] Under Vision Zero, the City uses every tool at its disposal to improve the safety of our streets, and bus priority projects often provide such opportunities. Bus bulbs shorten pedestrian crossings and improve bus operations. New crosswalks and median refuge islands can improve safety for all pedestrians, including bus riders accessing stops.
### [p025_c0005] Bus Stop Accessibility
[p025_c0006] In addition to creating safe crossing conditions, bus stops need to be accessible to everyone. This means that nearby sidewalks and pedestrian ramps are present and in good condition. NYCDOT ensures this is the case in all its bus priority projects.
### [p025_c0007] Turn Restrictions
[p025_c0008] Limiting certain turns can increase safety for all users. In certain projects, doing so also allows buses to move faster and avoid adverse interactions, including collisions with vehicles, pedestrians, bicyclists, and other buses. Turn restrictions also benefit traffic flow and relieve congestion.
[p025_c0009] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 25_

## Page 26

### [p026_c0001] Bus Priority Corridors
### [p026_c0002] Pelham Parkway, Fordham Road, and West 207 Street (Eastchester Avenue to Broadway)
### [p026_c0003] Background
[p026_c0004] Pelham Parkway, Fordham Road, and West 207 Street provide a critical east-west connection in the Bronx transportation network. Fordham Road is a bustling commercial corridor with numerous retail and dining destinations, in addition to major institutions such as Fordham University, the Bronx Zoo, and the New York Botanical Garden. The street varies between 50 feet and 70 feet wide, with two travel lanes in each direction and curbside bus lanes active during weekday peak hours. While the implementation of bus lanes in 2007 substantially improved bus service along the corridor, patterns have shifted over time and loading activities frequently block the bus lanes, slowing bus service and traffic. A reexamination of the design is warranted to see how existing bus lanes, travel lanes, and curb regulations might be updated to better serve bus riders and other needs along the corridor.
[p026_c0005] As part of the Final Plan, the majority of routes will maintain their existing alignment and frequency, with a few stop removals (including two on Fordham Road).
- [p026_c0006] • Corridor length: 3.1 miles • Routes served: Bx9, Bx12, Bx12 SBS, Bx17, Bx22, Bee Line 60-62 • Combined daily route ridership: 86,000
> [p026_c0007] A detailed map of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign, focusing on the Pelham Parkway, Fordham Road, and West 207 Street corridor. The map shows various bus routes in different colors, including Bx9 (red), Bx12 (blue), Bx12 SBS (green), Bx17 (orange), Bx22 (purple), and Bee Line 60-62 (yellow). Key landmarks and institutions are labeled, such as Fordham University, the Bronx Zoo, the New York Botanical Garden, and the Bronx Health Sciences Center. The map also shows the surrounding streets and neighborhoods, including Bedford Park, Morris Park, and University Heights. The map is oriented with North at the top.
[p026_c0008] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 26_

## Page 27

### [p027_c0001] Pelham Bay Park Station Area
### [p027_c0002] Background
[p027_c0003] Pelham Bay Park is the terminal of the 6 train in the Bronx, with connections to Orchard Beach, Co-op City, and Pelham Bay Park recreational area. The station sits adjacent to I-95/New England Thruway, with connections to Pelham Parkway and the Hutchinson River Parkway. Numerous bus routes converge at the Pelham Bay Park 6 Station; bus priority treatments in the area could help improve station access and egress, reducing bus travel times for riders.
- [p027_c0004] • Corridor length: 0.1 miles • Routes served: Bx5, Bx12, Bx12 SBS, Bx23, Bx24, Bx29, Q50 LTD • Combined daily route ridership: 63,000
> [p027_c0005] A detailed map of the Pelham Bay Park Station area in the Bronx. The map highlights the convergence of several bus routes at the station. [p027_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 27_

## Page 28

### [p028_c0001] Washington Bridge and West 181 Street (University Avenue to Broadway)
### [p028_c0002] Background
[p028_c0003] Washington Bridge and West 181 Street are critical transit links that connect neighborhoods from all over the Bronx with Washington Heights in Upper Manhattan. The five bus routes that traverse the bridge and West 181 Street provide subway connections, access to major commercial districts, and inter-city transit connections at the George Washington Bridge Bus Terminal. Given its location adjacent to the George Washington Bridge and the Cross-Bronx Expressway, along with its high commercial density, the corridor is highly congested at all times of day.
[p028_c0004] West 181 Street is 50 feet wide with one travel lane in each direction, a center turning lane, and curbside parking lanes on both sides. In the afternoon rush hour, the eastbound curbside lane becomes a bus only lane. West 181 Street crosses the Harlem River over the Washington Bridge, after which the Bx11, Bx13, and Bx35 buses head south on E.L. Grant Highway and the Bx3 and Bx36 head north on University Avenue. While West 181 Street will retain all existing bus stops, increased frequency on both the Bx11 and Bx13 (to 8 minutes or better all-day) will send more buses through this highly congested corridor, necessitating additional transit priority treatments.
- [p028_c0005] • Corridor length: 0.8 miles • Routes served: Bx3, Bx11, Bx13, Bx35, Bx36 • Combined daily route ridership: 73,000
> [p028_c0006] A map of the Washington Bridge and West 181 Street corridor. The map shows the bridge crossing the Harlem River, with West 181 Street running along its length. Five bus routes are highlighted: Bx1 (red), Bx3 (orange), Bx11 (yellow), Bx13 (blue), Bx35 (purple), and Bx36 (green). The map also shows surrounding streets like Broadway, W 181 St, W 179 St, and University Avenue. Landmarks such as Yeshiva University, Washington Bridge, and Morris Heights are labeled. The map is oriented with North at the top.
[p028_c0007] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 28_

## Page 29

### [p029_c0001] East 149 Street (River Avenue to Southern Boulevard)
### [p029_c0002] Background
[p029_c0003] East 149 Street is a major crosstown street and continuous retail corridor from the 145 Street Bridge through the South Bronx neighborhoods of Mott Haven, Melrose, Woodstock, and The Hub shopping district. The street is 60 to 70 feet wide and includes two travel lanes in each direction, metered parking on both sides of the street, and a narrow concrete median on some blocks. Traffic is heavy due to 145 Street Bridge traffic to and from Manhattan and double parking in front of retailers.
- [p029_c0004] • Corridor length: 1.5 miles • Routes served: Bx19, Bx2, Bx4A, Bx17 • Combined daily route ridership: 46,000 (excluding Bx2 ridership, for which ridership figures are combined with Bx1)
> [p029_c0005] A detailed map of the East 149 Street corridor in the South Bronx. The map highlights the street's path from the 145 Street Bridge in the northwest to Southern Boulevard in the southeast. Key landmarks include the 145 Street Bridge, the 149 Street Grand Concourse, the Home Community College, Lincoln Hospital, and The Hub shopping district. Major streets shown include River Avenue, Grand Concourse, Melrose Avenue, Westchester Avenue, and Southern Boulevard. [p029_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 29_

## Page 30

### [p030_c0001] E.L. Grant Highway (Cross Bronx Expressway to East 167 Street)
### [p030_c0002] Background
[p030_c0003] E.L. Grant Highway is a southern continuation of University Avenue, connecting Washington Heights with High Bridge and Grand Concourse, then shifting east at Jerome Avenue to become East 167 Street. It is a wide boulevard with a bike lane, two travel lanes, and curbside parking in each direction. The Final Plan proposes increased frequency on both the Bx11 and the Bx13 to 8 minutes or better all day. More frequent service will mean more buses traversing the corridor, necessitating bus priority improvements along this major north-south connector.
- [p030_c0004] • Corridor length: 0.6 miles • Routes served: Bx11, Bx13, Bx35 • Combined daily route ridership: 36,000
> [p030_c0005] A map of the E.L. Grant Highway corridor in the Bronx. The map shows the highway running north-south, connecting Washington Heights to High Bridge. Key streets shown include Ogdena V, Plimpton Av, Edward Av, Jerome Av, and East 167 St. Bus routes are color-coded: Bx35 (purple), Bx36 (red), Bx18 (green), Bx13 (blue), and Bx11 (orange). The map also shows the Harlem River to the west and various other streets and landmarks like Mt Eden Av, Macoma, and Bronx Leba Hospital. The map is a detailed view of the area around the E.L. Grant Highway, showing the proposed bus network and surrounding infrastructure.
[p030_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 30_

## Page 31

### [p031_c0001] University Avenue (Kingsbridge Road to Cross Bronx Expressway)
### [p031_c0002] Background
[p031_c0003] University Avenue is a major north-south corridor that connects neighborhoods in the western Bronx such as Kingsbridge, University Heights, Morris Heights, and High Bridge. University Avenue is mostly a standard 60-foot wide street with two travel lanes in each direction and unmetered curbside parking on both sides of the street. University Avenue widens south of Tremont Avenue to include two travel lanes and a bike lane in each direction, as well as a tree-lined median pedestrian mall. In addition to the Bx3, which runs the full length of the study corridor, the Bx18 and Bx36 also share portions of the corridor. The high number of buses converging on this north-south street make it an important area for bus priority improvements.
- [p031_c0004] • Corridor length: 2 miles • Routes served: Bx3, Bx18, Bx36 • Combined daily route ridership: 39,000
> [p031_c0005] A detailed map of the Bronx, New York, focusing on the University Avenue corridor. The map shows the street grid, including University Avenue, Kingsbridge Road, Morris Avenue, and Tremont Avenue. Major landmarks such as Kingsbridge College, Morris Heights Community College, and Herbert H. Lehman College are labeled. The map highlights several bus routes: Bx3 (red), Bx18 (green), and Bx36 (purple). Other bus routes like 12, 32, 41, and 44 are also visible. The map shows the intersection of University Avenue with various other streets and the proximity of the Cross Bronx Expressway to the south.
[p031_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 31_

## Page 32

### [p032_c0001] Tremont Avenue (Sedgwick Avenue to Boston Road)
### [p032_c0002] Background
[p032_c0003] Tremont Avenue is a major east-west corridor in the Central Bronx, connecting dense residential neighborhoods, neighborhood retail and dining, and parks. The street varies between 50 feet and 70 feet wide throughout the corridor. West of West Farms Square, Tremont Avenue has one travel lane in each direction, turning lanes, bike lanes, and parking lanes on either side. East of West Farms Square, Tremont Avenue has two travel lanes in each direction, left turn lanes, and pedestrian islands. Currently, the Bx36, Bx40, and Bx42 crisscross at Tremont Avenue/Webster Avenue and East 180 Street/Tremont Avenue. As part of the proposed improvements in the Final Plan, the Bx36 will run on Tremont Avenue continuously between East 180 Street and Webster Avenue, and the Bx40 and Bx42 will run on East 180 Street between Tremont Avenue and Webster Avenue to allow for more direct routing.
- [p032_c0004] • Corridor length: 6.8 miles • Routes served: Bx4A, Bx9, Bx18, Bx36, Bx40, Bx42 • Combined daily route ridership: 69,000
> [p032_c0005] A detailed map of the Tremont Avenue corridor in the Central Bronx. The map highlights several bus routes: Bx40 (blue), Bx18 (green), Bx36 (purple), Bx41 (dark blue), Bx9 (orange), and Bx19 (dark purple). The routes are shown as colored lines with numbers indicating the route ID. The map also shows the intersection of Tremont Avenue with East 180 Street and Webster Avenue. Surrounding areas include the Peter Jay Shaff Borthouse, Metro-North Morris Heights, River Park Towers, Morris Heights, Tremont, Crotona Park, and the Bronx Art Center. The map also shows various streets and landmarks, including West Farms Square, West Farms Park, and the Bronx Zoo.
[p032_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 32_

## Page 33

### [p033_c0001] East 167 Street & East 168 Street (Jerome Avenue to Franklin Avenue)
### [p033_c0002] Background
[p033_c0003] East 167 Street and East 168 Street provide an important crosstown connection for riders of the Bx35. Both streets are approximately 50 feet wide, with one travel lane and one bike lane in each direction. The street is busy and often congested throughout the day, serving a mix of retail, multiple schools, and dense surrounding neighborhoods. Buses are regularly delayed by traffic queues and would benefit from targeted bus priority improvements. Both East 167 Street and East 168 Street are Vision Zero Priority Corridors within a Vision Zero Priority Area.
- [p033_c0004] • Corridor length: 1.2 miles • Routes served: Bx35 • Daily route ridership: 27,000
> [p033_c0005] A detailed map of the Bronx, New York, highlighting the proposed bus network redesign for East 167 Street and East 168 Street. The map shows a grid of streets with various bus routes marked. East 167 Street and East 168 Street are highlighted in blue and orange, respectively, indicating they are Vision Zero Priority Corridors. The map includes labels for major landmarks such as Yankee Stadium, the Bronx Museum of the Arts, and the High Bridge. It also shows the locations of bus stops and routes, including the Bx35 route. The map is oriented with North at the top, and the streets are labeled with their names and directions (e.g., E 167 ST, W 168 ST).
[p033_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 33_

## Page 34

### [p034_c0001] Story Avenue (Bronx River Avenue to White Plains Road)
### [p034_c0002] Background
[p034_c0003] Story Avenue is an important east-west corridor serving the Soundview neighborhood, with Bx5 service currently providing connections to nearby subway lines. As part of the Final Plan, the Bx6 SBS will be rerouted to follow Bruckner Boulevard to Bronx River Avenue and Story Avenue, which will provide Soundview with additional bus service and more extensive crosstown connections.
[p034_c0004] Story Avenue is approximately 50 feet wide, with one travel lane in each direction. The curb is currently signed with alternate side parking on both sides of the street, with some No Standing zones near schools, parks, and fire stations. Traffic becomes heavily congested with long traffic queues, leading to slow bus speeds and delays.
- [p034_c0005] • Corridor length: 1.4 miles • Routes served: Bx5 (existing), Bx6 SBS (after redesign) • Combined daily route ridership: 32,000
> [p034_c0006] A map of the Bronx area showing the proposed bus network redesign. The map highlights the rerouting of the Bx6 SBS route. The route is shown as a thick blue line that follows Bruckner Boulevard, then turns south onto Bronx River Avenue, and finally runs east along Story Avenue. The map also shows the existing Bx5 route in red, which runs along Story Avenue and connects to the subway. Other major roads shown include Bruckner Boulevard, Bronx River Avenue, Lafayette Avenue, and White Plains Road. The Soundview neighborhood is labeled, along with local landmarks like Hunts Point and the Bronx River. The map also indicates the locations of various bus stops and subway stations.
[p034_c0007] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 34_

## Page 35

### [p035_c0001] East Gun Hill Road (Bainbridge Avenue to Bartow Avenue)
### [p035_c0002] Background
[p035_c0003] East Gun Hill Road is a major crosstown street covering the northeast Bronx neighborhoods of Norwood, Williamsbridge, Pelham Gardens, and Baychester, with routes connecting to Co-op City and the Bay Plaza Mall. The street is 60 feet wide and includes two travel lanes in each direction and metered parking on both sides. The Final Plan proposes rerouting the Bx30 onto Boston Road, and increasing Bx28 and Bx38 service. More frequent bus service further necessitates bus priority along this heavily congested east-west corridor.
- [p035_c0004] • Corridor length: 2.3 miles • Routes served: Bx28, Bx30, Bx38 • Combined daily route ridership: 23,000
> [p035_c0005] A detailed map of the East Gun Hill Road corridor in the northeast Bronx. The map highlights the street's path from Bainbridge Avenue in the west to Bartow Avenue in the east. Key neighborhoods shown include Norwood, Williamsbridge, Pelham Gardens, Baychester, and Eastchester. Major landmarks such as the Central Bronx Complex, Metropolitan Hospital, and the Bay Plaza Shopping Center are marked. The map also shows the locations of the Metro North North Williamsbridge station and the MTA bus stops for routes 28, 30, and 38. The street grid, including Gun Hill Road, Boston Road, and various local streets, is clearly depicted.
[p035_c0006] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 35_

### [p036_c0001] 4. ROUTE-LEVEL IMPROVEMENTS
- [p036_c0002] ◆ Regular Bus Service ◆ Express Bus Service

## Page 37

### [p037_c0001] ROUTE-LEVEL IMPROVEMENTS
### [p037_c0002] Regular Bus Service
[p037_c0003] Finalized recommendations at the route level will establish frequent service along key corridors while we work with our partners at NYCDOT to implement bus priority measures on those same corridors. Route alignment changes will make service simpler and more direct whenever possible, while also ensuring that concerns and comments from customers have been incorporated.
[p037_c0004] Of the 46 Local, Limited, and SBS routes that operate in the Bronx or out of a Bronx bus depot, we finalized modifications to 16 routes, with two new routes added, the Bx25 and the M125. The finalized individual route proposals (beginning on page 44) highlight what changed, if anything, with the release of the Final Plan.
[p037_c0005] The following table identifies what improvements have been made to each regular bus service route.

## Page 39

### [p039_c0001] Express Bus Service
[p039_c0002] We propose making route-level improvements for several express bus routes. Like regular bus service recommendations, finalized express bus changes aim to streamline service and make express routes simpler and more direct. Some recommendations call for service level reductions to run more direct, effective, and efficient express bus service.
[p039_c0003] Of the 11 express bus routes that operate in the Bronx, we finalized modifications to six routes and introduced one new route. All finalized individual route proposals (beginning on page 138) highlight what changed, if anything, with the release of the Final Plan.
[p039_c0004] The following table identifies what improvements have been made to each express bus service route.
[p039_c0005]

> [p040_c0002] A large, stylized number 5 is centered on a solid orange background. The number 5 is rendered in a lighter shade of orange, creating a subtle contrast with the background. ## Page 41

### [p041_c0001] NEXT STEPS: OUTREACH AND IMPLEMENTATION
[p041_c0002] Following release of this Final Plan, we will be out and about in the Bronx to hear from you.
[p041_c0003] Redesigning a bus network is a collaborative process and cannot work without comments and feedback from our customers. As you read through each individual route profile and the appendices that follow, think about what these changes mean for you. We need your input and hope to see you at an outreach event this fall. You can always submit a comment on the project website.
[p041_c0004] Detailed information about the following public input sessions will be on the project website :
- [p041_c0005] • Community Board Presentations • On-street Pop-up events • Info Sessions at subway stations • Virtual Open House
[p041_c0006] Final Plan report promoted on digital screens, on social media at #BronxBusRedesign, and in literature distributed on buses.
[p041_c0007] Following these events, we will prepare for implementation. We have allotted ample time to gather feedback and ensure that any changes made will be done so with clarity and transparency, and will be easily accessible for review before taking effect. You will continue to hear from us as we get closer to implementation.
[p041_c0008] Additional key dates include:
### [p041_c0009] Winter/Spring 2020
- [p041_c0010] • Public Hearing on Plan • MTA Board Votes on Plan
### [p041_c0011] Summer/Fall 2020
- [p041_c0012] • Plan to Be Implemented

> [p041_c0014] A photograph of two people, a man and a woman, standing next to a blue outreach van in the rain. Both are wearing orange and yellow safety vests. ## Page 43

### [p043_c0001] Bx1 Local and Limited
### [p043_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p043_c0003] Route
[p043_c0004] The Bx1 routing will not change. The route is already straight, direct, and connects to several important destinations and transfer points. The Bx1 Limited's routing also will not change.
[p043_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx2, Bx6, Bx6 Select Bus Service, Bx12, Bx12 Select Bus Service, Bx19, Bx40, and Bx42.
### [p043_c0006] Stops
[p043_c0007] Three percent (3 of 93) of the Bx1 stops will be removed, improving the average distance between stops from 861 feet to 890 feet. Three percent (2 of 53) of the Bx1 Limited stops will be removed, improving the average distance between Limited stops from 1,523 feet to 1,584 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p043_c0008] See full stop list on page 176.
### [p043_c0009] Schedule
[p043_c0010] The Bx1 schedule will not change. Both the Bx1 Local and Bx1 Limited will have the same service frequencies and spans as they currently do, as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Where the Bx1 and Bx2 overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will be 8 minutes or better.
### [p043_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p043_c0012]

### [p049_c0001] Bx4 Local
### [p049_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p049_c0003] Route
[p049_c0004] The Bx4 routing will not change. The route is already straight and direct.
[p049_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx19, Bx27, Bx35, Bx36, Bx39, and Q44 Select Bus Service.
[p049_c0006] Note: though the Bx4 routing will not change, the Bx4A routing will be changing.
### [p049_c0007] Stops
[p049_c0008] Ten percent (6 of 60) of the Bx4 stops will be removed, improving the average distance between stops from 808 feet to 900 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p049_c0009] See full list on page 186.
### [p049_c0010] Schedule
[p049_c0011] The Bx4 weekday schedule will improve to 15 minutes or better all day. The shortening of the Bx4A frees up resources we will use to increase service frequency on both the Bx4 and Bx4A. Where the two routes overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will be 8 minutes or better. Weekend frequencies will also improve, as shown below. Due to the Bx4A routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

## Page 51

### [p051_c0001] Bx4A Local
### [p051_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p051_c0003] Route
[p051_c0004] The Bx4A routing will change. The new Bx4A will travel from Westchester Square to Southern Boulevard, using its current routing via Metropolitan Avenue and Westchester Avenue. The Bx4 routing will remain unchanged, with service from Westchester Avenue to The Hub maintained.
[p051_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx19, Bx27, Bx35, Bx36, Bx39, and Q44 Select Bus Service.
### [p051_c0006] Stops
[p051_c0007] Nineteen percent (9 of 48) of the Bx4A stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 762 feet to 943 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p051_c0008] See full list on page 188.
### [p051_c0009] Schedule
[p051_c0010] The shortening of the Bx4A frees up resources we will use to increase service frequency on both the Bx4 and Bx4A. Where the two routes overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will be 8 minutes or better. Weekend frequencies will also improve, as shown below.

### [p053_c0001] Bx5 Local
### [p053_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p053_c0003] Route
[p053_c0004] The Bx5 routing will not change. The existing route is relatively direct, operates in neighborhoods that are far from subway service, and connects to several important transfer points. The Bx5 will continue to serve Bay Plaza on weekends.
[p053_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx6, Bx6 Select Bus Service, Bx12 Select Bus Service, Bx19, and Bx35.
### [p053_c0006] Stops
[p053_c0007] Thirteen percent (9 of 69) of the Bx5 stops will be removed, improving the average distance between stops from 1,154 feet to 1,330 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p053_c0008] See full list on page 190.
### [p053_c0009] Schedule
[p053_c0010] The Bx5 weekday and weekend schedule will receive a slight decrease in frequency to reallocate resources for the new Bx6 Select Bus Service extension along Story Avenue. With both the Bx5 and Bx6 SBS combined, Story Avenue will now have a bus scheduled every 3 minutes in the weekday AM peak, every 6 minutes in the midday, and every 4 minutes in the PM peak. Ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

[p053_c0013] *Frequencies are slightly decreased in order to reallocate resources to the NEW Bx6-SBS extension along Story Av. (combined Bx5 and Bx6-SBS frequencies on Story Av are significantly better than existing Bx5 alone)

### [p057_c0003] Route
[p057_c0004] The Bx6 Select Bus Service routing will change. To improve crosstown connections, the Bx6 Select Bus Service will be rerouted along Bruckner Boulevard, Bronx River Avenue, and Story Avenue to a new eastern terminal at Turnbull and Pugsley avenues. The route will no longer serve Hunts Point, which will continue to be served by Bx6 Local Service. This new routing will introduce additional connections for Bx5 riders and will provide faster crosstown service along Story Avenue for Soundview residents.
[p057_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx5, Bx6, Bx13, Bx15, and Bx19.
### [p057_c0006] Stops
[p057_c0007] No bus stops will be removed, apart from those along the discontinued segment serving Hunts Point. However, ten new stops will be added to accommodate the proposed segment serving Story Avenue and terminating at Turnbull and Pugsley avenues. The Bx6 SBS average distance between stops will remain 2,285 feet.
[p057_c0008] See full list on page 194.
### [p057_c0009] Schedule
[p057_c0010] The Bx6 SBS schedule will not change. The Bx6 SBS will have the same service frequency and span as it currently does, as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Where the Bx6 SBS and Bx6 Local overlap, the combined frequency will remain the same. Where the Bx6 SBS and Bx5 overlap on Story Avenue, the combined weekday frequency will be every 3 minutes in the AM peak, every 6 minutes in the midday, and every 4 minutes in the PM peak. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

## Page 67

### [p067_c0001] Bx11 Local
### [p067_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p067_c0003] Route
[p067_c0004] The Bx11 routing will change as part of an effort to simplify the Bx11, Bx18, Bx35, Bx36, Bx40, and Bx42 routes. By streamlining routes, reducing the number of turns, avoiding slow speed segments, and improving stop spacing, customers will see improved reliability and bus speed. The Bx11 will now serve East 174 Street and terminate in the eastbound direction at the Parkchester 6 Station. The extended Bx35 will serve Jennings Street and West Farms Road. To allow the Bx11 to travel directly into Manhattan via Edward L. Grant Highway, the extended Bx18 will replace the existing Bx11 service to Shakespeare Avenue, West 168 Street, Ogden Avenue, and Plimpton Avenue.
### [p067_c0005] Stops
[p067_c0006] Twenty-one percent (14 of 66) of the Bx11 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving the average distance between stops from 807 feet to 1,028 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p067_c0007] See full list on page 210.
### [p067_c0008] Schedule
[p067_c0009] The Bx11 weekday schedule will be improved to 8 minutes or better all day. Additionally, due to the new route alignment along East 174 Street to Parkchester, the Bx11 will now have overnight service on both weeknights and weekends. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.
### [p067_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p067_c0011]

```text
Bx11 Local Toward GW Bridge (Westbound) Toward Parkchester (Eastbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 24 hours 24 hours 5 8 6 8 40 Saturdays 24 hours 24 hours 12 10 9 12 40 Sundays 24 hours 24 hours 17 12 11 15 40
```
[p067_c0012] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change
[p067_c0013] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 67_

## Page 75

### [p075_c0001] Bx15 Local and Limited
[p075_c0002]

```text
Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
```
### [p075_c0003] Route
[p075_c0004] The existing Bx15 will be split into two routes to improve reliability and bus speeds throughout the length of the route. The new Bx15 Local and Limited service will operate between The Hub and Fordham Plaza at all times, as it currently does on weekdays. The new M125 route will replace service along 125 Street to The Hub. The new Bx15 will thus avoid the traffic delays and reliability issues originating on 125 Street.
[p075_c0005] Key connecting routes include: the Bx9, Bx12 Select Bus Service, Bx19, Bx21, Bx36, and Bx41 Select Bus Service.
### [p075_c0006] Stops
[p075_c0007] Twenty-one percent (8 of 39) of the Bx15 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 967 feet to 1,225 feet. Fourteen percent (3 of 21) of the Bx15 Limited stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 1,838 feet to 2,163 feet.
[p075_c0008] See full list on page 218.
### [p075_c0009] Schedule
[p075_c0010] The weekday Bx15 Local and Limited schedules will be adjusted slightly due to ridership trends and the routing change introduced by the new M125. However, the combined frequencies of the Bx15 Local and Bx15 Limited will remain the same, as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Overnight frequencies have been decreased from every 20 minutes to every 30 minutes to match ridership, and because the portion of the route on 125th Street in Manhattan will now be covered by the M125. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.
### [p075_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p075_c0012]

```text
Bx15 Local Toward The Hub (Southbound) Toward 3 Av-Fordham Plz (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 24 hours 24 hours 8 12 9 10 30 Saturdays 24 hours 24 hours 8 8 7 8 30 Sundays 24 hours 24 hours 11 9 9 9 30
```

## Page 81

### [p081_c0001] Bx18 Local
[p081_c0002]

```text
Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
```
### [p081_c0003] Route
[p081_c0004] The Bx18 will be extended to serve a new section along 168th Street and Shakespeare Avenue, replacing the Bx11 along this segment. In combination with frequency improvements, Bx18 riders will have better access to the East 170 Street 4 and B D stations, and a new direct connection between the HighBridge and Morris Heights neighborhoods. The route will operate as a circulator, running both clockwise and counter-clockwise throughout its length.
[p081_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx1, Bx2, Bx3, Bx11, and Bx36.
### [p081_c0006] Stops
[p081_c0007] Nineteen percent (10 of 53) of the Bx18 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 705 feet to 873 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p081_c0008] See full list on page 224.
### [p081_c0009] Schedule
[p081_c0010] The Bx18 weekday and weekend schedules will be improved. Because it will serve as a new HighBridge/Morris Heights circulator and as a replacement for the Bx11 along 168th Street and Shakespeare Avenue, the Bx18 frequencies and spans have been increased, both in the clockwise and counter-clockwise directions. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.
### [p081_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p081_c0012]

### [p093_c0001] Bx24 Local
### [p093_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p093_c0003] Route
[p093_c0004] The Bx24 routing will change with the elimination of a short, meandering segment within Country Club along Ohm Avenue, Griswold Drive, and Spencer Drive. While some Bx24 riders will experience minimal disruptions, the majority will benefit from faster bus speeds and more reliable service, due to the reduction in turns.
[p093_c0005] Note: The Draft Plan proposal to shorten the Bx8 and replace its service to Throgs Neck with the Bx24 will not be implemented. Instead, the Bx8 will maintain its existing routing and the Bx24 routing will experience a minor change within Country Club only.
[p093_c0006] Key connecting routes include: Bx8, Bx12, Bx12 Select Bus Service, Bx40, Bx42, and Q50 Limited.
### [p093_c0007] Stops

## Page 95

### [p095_c0001] Bx25 Local
### [p095_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p095_c0003] Route
[p095_c0004] The Bx25 is a new route serving Co-op City and the eastern Bronx. Outside Co-op City, the Bx25 will follow the same routing as the Bx26 along Allerton Avenue. Within Co-op City, the Bx25 will follow the same routing as the Bx38, traveling on Baychester Avenue and Co-op City Boulevard before terminating at the Bay Plaza Shopping Center in the eastbound direction.
[p095_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx1, Bx2, Bx8, Bx10, Bx31, Bx34, Bx39, and Bx41 Select Bus Service.
### [p095_c0006] Stops
[p095_c0007] No stops unique to the Bx25 will be removed, as it is a new route. However, the Bx25 will reflect the stops removed from the Bx26 and Bx38, respectively. Nineteen percent (16 of 83) of these stops will be removed, giving the Bx25 an average stop spacing of 1,114 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p095_c0008] See full list on page 238.
### [p095_c0009] Schedule
[p095_c0010] The Bx25 and Bx26 will have the same combined service frequencies and spans as the existing Bx26 on Allerton Avenue. However, the service in Co-op City will alternate between the two routes, making every other trip a Bx25 trip. While this splits the frequencies to Section 5 in half, it provides a new direct connection from the northern sections to the Bedford Park area. Where the two routes overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will still be 15 minutes or better. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.
### [p095_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p095_c0012]

```text
Bx25 Local Toward Paul Av (Westbound) Toward Bay Plaza (Eastbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:45 am - 10:45 pm 6:30 am - 11:30 pm 17* 24* 18* 24* - Saturdays 6:00 am - 10:45 pm 7:00 am - 11:45 pm 30* 30* 30* 30* - Sundays 6:30 am - 10:15 pm 7:15 am - 11:15 pm 30* 30* 30* 30* -
```
[p095_c0013] *Service on Allerton Avenue has not been reduced, but rather, split with the NEW Bx25 to the northern sections of Co-op City; the frequencies shown here are at Bay Plaza.
[p095_c0014] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change
[p095_c0015] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 95_

### [p099_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p099_c0003] Route
[p099_c0004] The Bx27 routing will not change. The existing route connects to several important destinations and exhibits good performance metrics.
[p099_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx4, Bx5, Bx11, Bx19, and Bx35.
### [p099_c0006] Stops
[p099_c0007] Ten percent (5 of 50) of the Bx27 stops will be removed, improving the average distance between stops from 714 feet to 795 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p099_c0008] See full list on page 242.
### [p099_c0009] Schedule
[p099_c0010] The Bx27 schedule will not change. The Bx27 will have the same service frequency and span as it currently does, as of the Fall 2019 schedule.

## Page 101

### [p101_c0001] Bx28 Local
### [p101_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p101_c0003] Route
[p101_c0004] The Bx28 routing will change on the western end of the route. In Norwood and Bedford Park, service will be discontinued on Mosholu Parkway and Paul Avenue. Instead, the route will be made more direct by operating service on Bainbridge Avenue and Bedford Park Boulevard.
[p101_c0005] Note: The Draft Plan proposal to terminate the route at Asch Loop in the eastbound direction will not be implemented. The Bx28 will maintain its existing routing in Co-op City.
[p101_c0006] Key connecting routes include: Bx1, Bx2, Bx8, Bx10, Bx30, Bx31, Bx36, Bx39, and Bx41 Select Bus Service.
### [p101_c0007] Stops
[p101_c0008] Seventeen percent (15 of 89) of the Bx28 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 785 feet to 947 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p101_c0009] See full list on page 244.
### [p101_c0010] Schedule
[p101_c0011] The Bx28 weekday schedule will improve moderately. To make up for the loss of the Bx30 from Gun Hill Road, weekday frequencies will improve to match expected ridership. Spans of service and weekend frequencies will remain as they are, as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Where the Bx28 and Bx38 overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will be 8 minutes or better.
### [p101_c0012] Span of Service and Frequency
[p101_c0013]

```text
Bx28 Local Toward Fordham (Westbound) Toward Co-op City Section 5 (Eastbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 24 hours 24 Hours 10 15 11 13 40 Saturdays 24 hours 24 Hours 20 17 16 20 40 Sundays 24 hours 24 Hours 30 20 20 20 40
```
[p101_c0014] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change

## Page 103

### [p103_c0001] Bx29 Local
### [p103_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p103_c0003] Route
[p103_c0004] The Bx29 routing will change. The route will be shortened, with its northbound terminal moved to the Pelham Bay Park 6 Station.
[p103_c0005] Key connections include: Bx5, Bx12, Bx12 Select Bus Service, Bx23, Bx24, and Q50 Limited.
### [p103_c0006] Stops
[p103_c0007] Twenty-eight percent (8 of 29) of the Bx29 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 1,480 feet to 2,072 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p103_c0008] See full list on page 246.
### [p103_c0009] Schedule
[p103_c0010] The Bx29 schedule will improve. While the Bx29 weekday and weekend frequencies will not change, the route will now provide overnight service to and from City Island. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

```text
Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
```

### [p105_c0003] Route
[p105_c0004] The Bx30 routing will change. Instead of operating on East Gun Hill Road, the route's Boston Road service will extend all the way from Conner Street to Pelham Parkway. The new routing will provide new connections to and from the Pelham Pkwy 2 5 Station and the Bx12 Local and Select Bus Service.
[p105_c0005] Note: The Draft Plan proposal to terminate the route at Asch Loop in the eastbound direction will not be implemented. The Bx30 will maintain its existing routing in Co-op City, while moving forward with the Draft Proposal to reroute service to Boston Road.
[p105_c0006] Key connecting routes include: Bx12, Bx12 Select Bus Service, Bx23, Bx25, Bx26, Bx28, Bx31, Bx38, and Bx39, and Q50 Limited.
### [p105_c0007] Stops
[p105_c0008] Seven percent (6 of 82) of the Bx30 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 896 feet to 968 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p105_c0009] See full list on page 248.
### [p105_c0010] Schedule
[p105_c0011] The Bx30 schedule will not change. The Bx30 will have the same service frequency and span as it currently does, as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

## Page 115

### [p115_c0001] Bx35 Local
### [p115_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p115_c0003] Route
[p115_c0004] The Bx35 routing will change as part of the larger redesign effort to improve crosstown service by streamlining the Bx11, Bx35, Bx36, Bx40, and Bx42. The new Bx35 will bypass the congestion at Gladstone Square to better serve West Farms Road, Jennings Street, and Bryant Avenue. This reroute supports the Bx11 service changes while improving reliability and coverage across all of the affected routes.
[p115_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx1, Bx2, Bx3, Bx4, Bx11, and Bx27.
### [p115_c0006] Stops
[p115_c0007] Fifteen percent (8 of 53) of Bx35 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 824 feet to 973 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p115_c0008] See full list on page 258.
### [p115_c0009] Schedule
[p115_c0010] The Bx35 schedule will not change. The Bx35 will have the same service frequency and span as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.
### [p115_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p115_c0012]

## Page 117

### [p117_c0001] Bx36 Local and Limited
### [p117_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p117_c0003] Route
[p117_c0004] The Bx36 routing will change as part of the larger redesign effort to improve crosstown service by streamlining the Bx11, Bx35, Bx36, Bx40, and Bx42. The new Bx36 will still travel between Soundview and Washington Heights, but will now operate on East Tremont Avenue instead of East 174 and East 180 Streets. The new routing will continue to serve the West Farms and East Tremont neighborhoods. However, it will avoid its existing indirect routing along Boston Road. Modified Bx11 and Bx40 routings will provide new crosstown service to riders on East 174 Street and on East 180 Street, respectively.
[p117_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx1, Bx2, Bx3, Bx9, Bx41 Select Bus Service, and Q44 Select Bus Service.
### [p117_c0006] Stops
[p117_c0007] Twenty-one percent (18 of 86) of Bx36 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 795 feet to 1,009 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p117_c0008] See full list on page 260.
### [p117_c0009] Schedule
[p117_c0010] The Bx36 schedule will not change. The Bx36 Local and Limited will have the same service frequency and span as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.
### [p117_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p117_c0012]


### [p119_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement

[p119_c0006] Key connecting routes include: Bx10, Bx28, Bx30, Bx31, Bx39, and Bx41 Select Bus Service.

[p119_c0009] See full list on page 262.
### [p119_c0010] Schedule
[p119_c0011] The Bx38 weekday schedule will improve moderately. To make up for the loss of the Bx30 from Gun Hill Road, weekday frequencies will be improved to match expected ridership. Spans of service and weekend frequencies will remain as they are in the Fall 2019 schedule. Where the Bx28 and Bx38 overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will be 8 minutes or better.

## Page 123

### [p123_c0001] Bx40 Local
- [p123_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p123_c0003] Route
[p123_c0004] The Bx40 routing will change as part of the larger redesign effort to improve crosstown service by streamlining the Bx11, Bx35, Bx36, Bx40, and Bx42. The Bx40 will still travel between Throgs Neck and Morris Heights, but will now do so via East Tremont Avenue and East 180 Street. The rerouted Bx36 and Bx36 Limited service will replace the existing Bx40 routing on Rosedale and Webster avenues. This redesigned routing will provide more direct service along East Tremont Avenue and East 180 Street, while avoiding the congestion around West Farms Square. A new connection to the E 180 St 2 5 station—an accessible station—will provide access to subway service.
[p123_c0005] Note: The Draft Plan proposal to adjust Bx40 service in Thros Neck will not be implemented.
[p123_c0006] Key connecting routes include: Bx1, Bx2, Bx15, Bx22, Bx36, and Bx42.
### [p123_c0007] Stops
[p123_c0008] Thirty-two percent (36 of 111) of Bx40 stops along the new alignment will be removed, improving stop spacing from 800 feet to 1,190 feet. By removing these stops, we'll improve reliability along the route.
[p123_c0009] See full list on page 266.
### [p123_c0010] Schedule
[p123_c0011] The Bx40 schedule will not change. The Bx40 will have the same service frequency and span as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Where the Bx40 and Bx42 overlap, the combined all-day weekday frequency will be 15 minutes or better. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

[p123_c0013]

- [p133_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p133_c0003] Route
[p133_c0004] The M100 routing will change. Service along 125 Street will be discontinued. The new southbound terminal will be at Amsterdam Avenue and West 125 Street. Congestion on 125 Street is the primary cause of reliability issues throughout the route, and service on the 125 Street segment is duplicated by the M60 Select Bus Service, M101, and new M125 routes.
[p133_c0005] Key connecting routes include: Bx3, Bx6 Select Bus Service, Bx7, Bx19, and Bx36.
### [p133_c0006] Stops

[p133_c0008] See full list on page 280.
### [p133_c0009] Schedule
[p133_c0010] The M100 schedule will not change. The M100 will have the same service frequency and span as of the Fall 2019 schedule. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

### [p135_c0001] M125 Local
[p135_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p135_c0003] Route
[p135_c0004] The M125 is a new route that will replace the southern portion of the Bx15 that runs along 125 Street in Manhattan and to The Hub via Willis Avenue. The new routing will preserve an important interborough connection and improve reliability for both routes created from the existing Bx15.
### [p135_c0005] Stops
[p135_c0006] The M125—where it will replace Bx15 service—will largely serve the same stops as the existing Bx15. However, 14 percent (7 of 49) of these Bx15 stops will be removed, improving the average distance between stops along this segment from 728 feet to 853 feet.
[p135_c0007] See full list on page 282.
### [p135_c0008] Schedule
[p135_c0009] As a new route replacing the M100 and Bx15 on 125 Street in Manhattan, the M125 will run 24 hours a day, with an all-day weekday frequency of 8 minutes or better. Due to the routing change, ridership will be closely monitored, and schedules will be adjusted accordingly.

[p135_c0011]

### [p139_c0003] Route
[p139_c0004] The BxM1 routing will not change. The existing route provides a direct connection between Riverdale and East Midtown.
### [p139_c0005] Stops
[p139_c0006] One BxM1 stop will be removed and one stop will be added. The average distance between stops will be 1,542 feet.
[p139_c0007] See full stop list on page 286.
### [p139_c0008] Schedule
[p139_c0009] The BxM1 schedule will change. The service span for Weekdays, Saturdays, and Sundays will be shortened, with service ending earlier in the day. The service span for Saturdays will begin earlier, an improvement from current service. The frequency of service will also be reduced on Weekdays and Saturdays. Sunday service will remain unchanged.
### [p139_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p139_c0011]

```text
BxM1 Toward E 34 St (Southbound) Toward 261 St (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:30 am - 4:45 pm 6:45 am - 12:45 am 11 30 14 30 - Saturdays 6:30 am - 6:30 pm 8:00 am - 12:00 am 60 60 60 60 - Sundays 8:30 am - 5:30 pm 10:00 am - 10:00 pm 60 60 60 60 -
```
[p139_c0012] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change

## Page 141

### [p141_c0001] BxM2
### [p141_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p141_c0003] Route
[p141_c0004] The BxM2 routing will change. Service will be rerouted from the Major Deegan Expressway to operate via Inwood and the Henry Hudson Parkway to serve West Midtown. The proposed change will minimize the time the bus spends on heavily congested local Manhattan streets. Customers who use stops south of West 72 Street will have a faster trip, as buses will operate on the Henry Hudson Parkway to West 79 Street instead of traveling on 5th Avenue and traversing through Central Park.
### [p141_c0005] Stops
[p141_c0006] No BxM2 stops will be removed along the new alignment and one stop will be added. The average distance between stops will be 1,374 feet.
[p141_c0007] See full stop list on page 288.
### [p141_c0008] Schedule
[p141_c0009] The BxM2 schedule will change. The service span for Weekdays, Saturdays, and Sundays will be shortened, with service ending earlier in the day. The service span for Sundays will begin earlier, an improvement from current service. The frequency of service will also be reduced on Weekdays and Saturdays. Sunday service will remain unchanged.
### [p141_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p141_c0011]

```text
BxM2 Toward W 34 St (Southbound) Toward 261 St (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 6:00 am - 3:00 pm 12:00 pm - 12:45 am 24 60 23 30 - Saturdays 6:30 am - 5:30 pm 12:15 pm - 12:15 am 60 60 60 60 - Sundays 7:30 am - 1:30 pm 3:15 pm - 11:15 pm 60 60 60 60 -
```
[p141_c0012] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change
[p141_c0013] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 141_

[p142_c0004] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 142_

## Page 143

### [p143_c0001] BxM3
### [p143_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p143_c0003] Route
[p143_c0004] The BxM3 routing will not change. The existing route provides a direct connection between Yonkers, Riverdale, Kingsbridge, and Midtown.
### [p143_c0005] Stops
[p143_c0006] Two BxM3 stops will be removed. The average distance between stops will be 1,902 feet.
[p143_c0007] See full stop list on page 290.
### [p143_c0008] Schedule
[p143_c0009] The BxM3 schedule will change. The service span for Weekdays and Saturdays will be shortened. The frequency of service will also be reduced on Weekdays. Sunday service will be discontinued.
### [p143_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p143_c0011]

```text
BxM3 Toward W 26 St (Southbound) Toward Getty Sq (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:30 am - 1:45 pm 3:00 pm - 12:00 am 30 60 26 60 - Saturdays 6:30 am - 2:30 pm 3:15 pm - 12:15 am 60 60 60 60 - Sundays - - - - - - -
```
[p143_c0012] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change
[p143_c0013] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 143_

## Page 144

### [p144_c0001] BxM3 Yonkers-Midtown via 5 Av
> [p144_c0002] The map illustrates the proposed BxM3 bus route connecting Yonkers to Midtown via 5th Avenue. The route is depicted with green lines: a solid line for the 'Existing routing' and a dashed line for the 'Existing nonstop segment'. The route begins in Yonkers, following Broadway and Van Cortlandt, then turns south on Sedgwick Ave and W 240th St. It crosses the Manhattan Bridge and continues south on W 136th St, W 124th St, and W 120th St. The route then turns east on 5th Ave and continues south through the Bronx, passing through Lenox Hill, Yonkers, and ending near the Hudson River. ## Page 145

### [p145_c0001] BxM4
### [p145_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p145_c0003] Route
[p145_c0004] The BxM4 routing will change to maintain service on the majority of Grand Concourse due to community feedback. Service north of Van Cortlandt Avenue East will be rerouted via Mosholu Parkway and Goulden Avenue to the new terminal at West 205 Street and Paul Avenue. Service along East 233 Street and Katonah Avenue will be provided by the new BxM5 route.
### [p145_c0005] Stops
[p145_c0006] No BxM4 stops will be removed along the new alignment. The average distance between stops will be 2,256 feet.
[p145_c0007] See full stop list on page 292.
### [p145_c0008] Schedule
[p145_c0009] The BxM4 schedule will change. Service will operate on Weekdays only, with service discontinued on Saturdays and Sundays. The service span on weekdays will operate during the peak periods only, at a frequency of every 30 minutes.
### [p145_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p145_c0011]

```text
BxM4 Toward W 26 St (Southbound) Toward W 205 St (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:30 am - 7:30 am 4:30 pm - 6:30 pm 30 - 30 - - Saturdays - - - - - - - Sundays - - - - - - -
```
[p145_c0012] Increased Service
[p145_c0013] Decreased Service
[p145_c0014] No Change

## Page 147

### [p147_c0001] BxM5
### [p147_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p147_c0003] Route
[p147_c0004] The BxM5 is a new route replacing the northern section of existing BxM4 service. The new route will begin in Mount Vernon at Mundy Lane/Pitman Avenue and travel via Nereid Av, Katonah Avenue, and East 233 Street onto the Major Deegan Expressway to existing BxM4 routing along 5th Avenue in Manhattan.
### [p147_c0005] Stops
[p147_c0006] Two BxM5 stops will be removed along the new alignment. The average distance between stops will be 2,099 feet.
[p147_c0007] See full stop list on page 294.
### [p147_c0008] Schedule
[p147_c0009] Service will operate weekdays during peak periods only, at a frequency of every 30 minutes.
### [p147_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p147_c0011]

```text
BxM5 Toward W 26 St (Southbound) Toward Sanford BI (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:30 am - 7:30 am 4:30 pm - 6:30 pm 30 - 30 - - Saturdays - - - - - - - Sundays - - - - - - -
```
[p147_c0012] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change

### [p151_c0003] Route
[p151_c0004] The BxM7 routing will not change. The existing route provides a direct connection between Co-op City and Midtown.

[p151_c0009] The BxM7 schedule will change. The service span for Weekdays, Saturdays, and Sundays will be shortened.
