[p154_c0003] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 154_

## Page 155

### [p155_c0001] BxM9
### [p155_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p155_c0003] Route
[p155_c0004] The BxM9 routing will not change. The existing route provides a direct connection between Throgs Neck and Midtown.
### [p155_c0005] Stops
[p155_c0006] Six BxM9 stops will be removed and four stops will be added. The average distance between stops will be 2,499 feet.
[p155_c0007] See full stop list on page 302.
### [p155_c0008] Schedule
[p155_c0009] The BxM9 schedule will change. Service spans will be shortened for Weekdays, Saturdays, and Sundays. The frequency of service for Weekdays and Saturdays will be reduced across all time periods. Sundays will remain unchanged.
### [p155_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p155_c0011]

```text
BxM9 Toward E 23 St (Southbound) Toward Throgs Neck (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 4:45 am - 3:00 pm 1:00 pm - 1:15 am 13 60 11 30 - Saturdays 6:15 am - 5:15 pm 1:00 pm - 12:00 am 60 60 60 60 - Sundays 7:15 am - 1:15 pm 3:30 pm - 11:30 pm 60 60 60 60 -
```
[p155_c0012] Increased Service
[p155_c0013] Decreased Service
[p155_c0014] No Change
[p155_c0015] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 155_

## Page 156

### [p156_c0001] BxM9 Throgs Neck-Midtown via 5 Av
> [p156_c0002] This map illustrates the proposed BxM9 bus route connecting Throgs Neck to Midtown via 5th Avenue. The route is depicted with a solid dark green line for 'Existing routing' and a dashed dark green line for 'Existing nonstop segment'. The route begins in Throgs Neck, following the Cross Bronx Expressway and Bruckner Expressway. It then crosses the Robert F. Kennedy Bridge into Manhattan, where it follows 5th Avenue through Midtown, passing through neighborhoods like Flatiron, Gramercy, Stuyvesant Town, and Greenpoint. The route continues south through the Bronx, passing through areas like North Side, Williamsburg, and East Williamsburg, before ending near the Navy Yard and Clinton Hill. ## Page 157

### [p157_c0001] BxM10
### [p157_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p157_c0003] Route
[p157_c0004] The BxM10 off-peak and weekend routing will change. Off-peak and weekend BxM10 service will operate via Hugh J. Grant Circle to serve current BxM6 customers who will no longer have off-peak and weekend service.
### [p157_c0005] Stops
[p157_c0006] Peak: No BxM10 stops will be removed and two stops will be added. The average distance between stops will be 2,395 feet.
[p157_c0007] Off-peak and Weekends: Three BxM10 stops will be removed and 11 stops will be added.
[p157_c0008] See full stop list on page 304.
### [p157_c0009] Schedule
[p157_c0010] The BxM10 schedule will change. Service spans will be shortened for Weekdays only with Saturdays and Sundays unchanged. The frequency of service for Weekdays will be reduced across all time periods. Saturdays and Sundays will remain unchanged.
### [p157_c0011] Span of Service and Frequency
[p157_c0012]

```text
BxM10 Toward E 23 St (Southbound) Toward Eastchester Rd (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:30 am - 10:00 pm 7:00 am - 12:15 am 15 60 14 30 - Saturdays 6:00 am - 11:00 pm 8:15 am - 12:15 am 30 30 30 30 - Sundays 7:00 am - 11:00 pm 8:15 am - 12:15 am 60 60 60 60 -
```
[p157_c0013] Increased Service
[p157_c0014] Decreased Service
[p157_c0015] No Change
[p157_c0016] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 157_

- [p158_c0002] Proposed Proposed nonstop segment
> [p158_c0003] The map illustrates the proposed BxM10 bus route in the Bronx. The route is depicted with a thick green line, with a dashed green line indicating a nonstop segment. The route begins at Williamsbridge and proceeds south through various neighborhoods, including Norwood, Bedford Park, and Olmsted Park. It then turns east, following Eastchester Rd and Morris Park Ave, before heading south through the High Bridge area and past the Robert F. Kennedy Bridge. ## Page 159

### [p159_c0001] BxM11
### [p159_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p159_c0003] Route
[p159_c0004] The BxM11 routing will change to operate from East 233 Street via Bronxwood Avenue and Boston Rd to existing BxM11 non-stop routing to Midtown. Service along White Plains Road will be discontinued to remove service that duplicates the subway and to provide faster, more direct service.
### [p159_c0005] Stops
[p159_c0006] No BxM11 stops will be removed. Sixteen stops will be added due to new route alignment. The average distance between stops will be 1,711 feet.
[p159_c0007] See full stop list on page 306.
### [p159_c0008] Schedule
[p159_c0009] The BxM11 schedule will change. Service spans will be shortened for Weekdays and Saturdays. Service spans for Sundays will begin earlier but also end earlier. The frequency of service for Weekdays and Saturdays will be reduced across all time periods with Sundays remaining unchanged.
### [p159_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p159_c0011]

```text
BxM11 Toward W 26 St (Southbound) Toward E 233 St (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:30 am - 1:00 pm 1:15 pm - 12:15 am 15 60 16 24 - Saturdays 6:30 am - 5:30 pm 9:00 am - 12:00 am 60 60 60 60 - Sundays 7:30 am - 5:30 pm 9:00 am - 11:00 pm 60 60 60 60 -
```
[p159_c0012] Increased Service
[p159_c0013] Decreased Service
[p159_c0014] No Change
[p159_c0015] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 159_

## Page 161

### [p161_c0001] BxM18
### [p161_c0002] Route Change Schedule Change Stop Change Change since Draft Plan Frequency Improvement
### [p161_c0003] Route
[p161_c0004] The BxM18 routing will change. Service will be rerouted from the Major Deegan Expressway and 5th Avenue to operate via Inwood and the Henry Hudson Parkway to serve Hudson Yards and Downtown. The proposed change will minimize the time the bus spends on heavily congested local Manhattan streets and provide Riverdale and Inwood customers with new fast, direct service to Hudson Yards.
### [p161_c0005] Stops
[p161_c0006] No BxM18 stops will be removed along the new alignment. The average distance between stops will be 1,554 feet.
[p161_c0007] See full stop list on page 308.
### [p161_c0008] Schedule
[p161_c0009] The BxM18 schedule will change. Service spans will begin earlier on Weekdays. The frequency of service for Weekdays will be reduced in the AM peak period. The PM peak period will remain unchanged.
### [p161_c0010] Span of Service and Frequency
[p161_c0011]

```text
Bx18 Toward South St (Southbound) Toward 261 St (Northbound) Avg. Frequency (Min.) AM Noon PM Eve Night Weekdays 5:45 am - 7:45 am 4:15 pm - 7:15 pm 20 - 30 - - Saturdays - - - - - - - Sundays - - - - - - -
```
[p161_c0012] ■ Increased Service ■ Decreased Service ■ No Change

### [p163_c0001] 7. APPENDICES
- [p163_c0002] ◆ Appendix 1 – Glossary of Terms ◆ Appendix 2 – Completed Public Outreach ◆ Appendix 3 – Individual Routes with Full Bus Stop List ◆ Appendix 4- Jobs and Residents Reachable Summary ◆ Appendix 5 – Weekday and Weekend Span and Frequency Tables

## Page 164

### [p164_c0001] APPENDIX 1 – GLOSSARY OF TERMS
[p164_c0002] Accessibility – a service, vehicle, or facility is accessible if it is in compliance with the ADA , or in general (nonlegal) terms if it is readily usable by persons with disabilities.
[p164_c0003] ADA – the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990, which applied in part to public transit , requires that transit providers must follow regulations ensuring that services, vehicles, and facilities are accessible to and usable by individuals with disabilities. See: accessibility
[p164_c0004] BRT – Bus Rapid Transit. BRT systems strive to bring faster, more reliable bus service to high ridership corridors by combining amenities of rail-based rapid transit systems with the flexibility of buses. New York City Transit’s implementation of BRT is Select Bus Service , which improves speed and reliability through dedicated bus lanes, off-board fare payment, stop spacing , and transit signal priority .
[p164_c0005] Boarding – entering or getting onto a bus, train, or other mode of transit.
[p164_c0006] Bus lane – a lane of the roadway dedicated exclusively to bus movement.
[p164_c0007] Bus network – a collection of bus routes, including the physical paths they take as well as their scheduled frequencies and spans of service. In essence, where buses travel, when buses travel, and how often buses travel.
[p164_c0008] Bus priority – any number of techniques or tools that enable bus transit to take precedence over other modes of surface transportation in traffic. With transit signal priority (TSP) , traffic lights can change more quickly from red to green or a green light can be held longer if a bus is approaching.
[p164_c0009] Bus stop balancing – improving stop spacing through removing and adjusting (moving) bus stops so that buses can travel more quickly along their routes. The thought process behind bus stop balancing is that buses currently stop too frequently; improvements in overall travel time and reliability will outweigh small increases in the time spent walking to bus stops.
[p164_c0010] Bus Time Pole Signs – real-time passenger information (RTPi) signs resembling standard bus stop lollipops but that are digitized and provide bus arrival time information.
[p164_c0011] CJTP – Customer Journey Time Performance. The percentage of customers whose journeys (trips) are completed within five minutes of the scheduled time. CJTP considers both how long customers wait at the bus stop beyond what they would have if their bus arrived on time, as well as how long customers spend on the bus beyond what they would have if the bus completed its trip in the time allotted in the schedule.
[p164_c0012] Connectivity – how well a transit network’s different bus and/or subway lines work together to ease, hasten, and expand transit options for riders.
[p164_c0013] Corridor – one or more roadways that connect to provide continuous travel. For example, Fordham Road and Pelham Parkway combine to form an east-west corridor in the Bronx.
[p164_c0014] Coverage service – bus service that operates at a minimum of every 30 minutes.
[p164_c0015] Crosstown – bus service operating primarily in an east-west travel pattern as opposed to a north-south pattern.
[p164_c0016] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 164_

## Page 165

[p165_c0001] Draft Plan – the second of three major reports released as part of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign. The Draft Plan presents initial redesign improvements that have subsequently shaped the recommendations in the Final Plan. Preceded by the Existing Conditions Report and followed by the Final Plan.
[p165_c0002] Existing Conditions Report – the first of three major reports released as part of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign. This report presents quantitative and qualitative analyses, including ridership and bus performance data, demographic data and maps, and profiles of each bus route in the Bronx. Followed by the Draft Plan and the Final Plan.
[p165_c0003] Express bus service – bus service focused specifically on transporting commuters between Manhattan and the outer boroughs. Express bus routes typically have a series of pick-up locations in one borough and a series of drop-off locations in the other, between which is an express segment. The bus does not stop throughout the express segment, which is generally on a highway.
[p165_c0004] Fast Forward Plan – New York City Transit’s 2018 strategic plan to modernize transit in New York City.
[p165_c0005] Frequency – the rate at which buses run along a specific route. See: headway
[p165_c0006] Grid route – routes that operate through multiple neighborhoods with customers boarding and alighting throughout the length of the route. Grid routes constitute more than eighty percent of New York City Transit’s local bus routes.
[p165_c0007] Headway – the scheduled interval of time between buses running along a specific route. See: frequency
[p165_c0008] Limited bus service – operates on the same routes served by local bus service, but makes fewer stops so as to travel the length of the route more quickly.
[p165_c0009] Local bus service – the most commonly provided bus service. Local bus service—in contrast to limited bus service—makes all stops along a route.
[p165_c0010] Low-performing – as it pertains to reducing service, low-performing routes are those that score lower in measures of productivity and ridership .
[p165_c0011] Market analysis – a study of all of the characteristics of the study area, such as: Who lives in the Bronx? Where in the Bronx do they live? Where do they work? How do they get there? If not for work or home, why do people visit the Bronx and where do they go? What will the Bronx look like in 20 years? See: Service analysis
[p165_c0012] MetroCard – the Metropolitan Transit Authority’s predominant fare payment method.
[p165_c0013] Network-level – in contrast with route-level , network-level improvements pertain to the Bronx Bus Network as a whole, rather than any individual route.
[p165_c0014] NYC DOT – New York City Department of Transportation
[p165_c0015] OMNY – the MTA’s new contactless fare payment system . Customers can use contactless debit and credit cards, as well as smart devices, to pay their fare. Full rollout of OMNY throughout the entire subway system and on all bus routes is expected by late 2020.
[p165_c0016] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 165_

## Page 166

[p166_c0001] Peak – the times during which commuter demand is heaviest and typically when the most service is provided. The morning peak period is weekdays between 7:00 AM and 9:00 AM. The afternoon peak period is weekdays between 4:00 PM and 7:00 PM.
[p166_c0002] Productivity – the measure of ridership given the level of service provided. Bus routes are more productive when they attract more riders per unit of time that they are in service.
[p166_c0003] Queue jump – queue jump lanes give buses priority at signalized intersections by providing buses the space (a dedicated lane) and time (a bus-specific, early green light) to enter traffic flow ahead of other vehicles.
[p166_c0004] Reliability – service reliability constitutes buses arriving at stops on time and at regular intervals, as well as customers completing their journey in the scheduled time frame. Our reliability metrics include measures of passenger wait times, on-time performance, and customer journey time performance at the borough-wide and route levels.
[p166_c0005] Ridership – the total number of customers using a specific route or the bus system generally.
[p166_c0006] Route-level – in contrast with network-level , route-level improvements pertain to individual bus routes rather than the Bronx Bus Network as a whole.
[p166_c0007] SBS – Select Bus Service. New York City Transit’s branded implementation of BRT (Bus Rapid Transit).
[p166_c0008] Service analysis – a study of the bus service delivered by NYCT and MTA Bus Company within the study area and how the service supports the Bronx’s residents, workers, and visitors. It also examines how the existing service compares with standards for bus service. See: Market analysis
[p166_c0009] Span – the time period throughout the day that a route is in service.
[p166_c0010] Stop spacing — the average traveled distance between bus stops along a route.
[p166_c0011] TNC – Transportation Network Company. Also known as ride-hailing service companies. TNC customers hail for-hire vehicles using mobile apps associated with various TNCs. Companies with a significant presence in New York City include Juno, Via, Uber, and Lyft.
[p166_c0012] Traffic signal improvements – See: bus priority
[p166_c0013] Transfer – the act of changing from one bus or subway line to another line to complete one’s trip. In most cases, the MTA allows one free transfer within two hours of the initial fare payment, with some exceptions. In some select cases, additional transfers are allowed. A transfer can also refer to the physical transfer receipt — or one-use MetroCard — used to validate the transfer.
[p166_c0014] TSP – Traffic Signal Priority. See: bus priority
[p166_c0015] Wait assessment – a measure of how evenly buses are spaced. It is defined as the percentage of actual intervals between buses that are no more than three minutes over the scheduled interval for the morning (6am-9am) and afternoon (4pm-7pm) peak periods, and no more than five minutes over the scheduled interval for the rest of the day.
[p166_c0016] Vision Zero – the City of New York’s plan to end traffic fatalities and injuries in New York City .
[p166_c0017] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 166_

## Page 167

### [p167_c0001] APPENDIX 2 - COMPLETED PUBLIC OUTREACH
[p167_c0002] Outreach and stakeholder engagement for the Bronx Bus Network Redesign began in 2018, shortly after the publication of Fast Forward: The Plan to Modernize New York City Transit .
[p167_c0003] Here is a summary of Bronx Bus Network Redesign outreach by the numbers:
- [p167_c0004] • 1 Update to the public timeline with explanation to support transparency • 2 Fast Forward Community Conversations • 3 Videos of our presentations to the Joint Borough Service Cabinet/Borough Board available on Bronxnet.org • 6 Workshops in fall 2018 to introduce the project and solicit feedback from customers • 9 Open Houses in spring and summer 2019 in the Bronx (8) and Upper Manhattan (1) • 13 On-street engagement events in 2019 • 64 Social media posts promoting the Bronx Bus Network Redesign • 200 Subway stations with digital screens ran digital messages systemwide at time of posting • 750 Online surveys completed in 2018 • 1,000 Survey cards distributed • 1,300 Comments received via webmail, phone, Twitter and mail • 1,300 Draft Plan surveys completed in 2019 • 2,000 Average views per social media post • 2,000 Intercept surveys completed in 2018 • 2,419 Digital screens on buses ran digital messages systemwide at time of posting • 7,000 Posters printed for distribution on buses and in subway stations • 16,000 Brochures handed out by our street team or distributed on buses • 39,154 unique project webpage views since September 2018
[p167_c0005] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 167_

## Page 168

### [p168_c0001] Draft Plan Outreach: May-September 2019
- [p168_c0002] • The Bronx Bus Network Redesign Draft Plan was published on May 31, 2019, at which time we began outreach for the Draft Plan, including a series of public input sessions, local and express bus surveys in English and Spanish, stakeholder meetings, and promotion across MTA digital screens and social media. • Eight Open Houses were held in the Bronx in June and one in Manhattan in August. Each open house offered attendees the opportunity to see proposed changes to bus service and speak one-on-one with MTA and NYCDOT staff. Over 800 people participated in the nine open houses. • A key goal of this phase of outreach was to promote the local and express bus surveys to our customers. During July and August, MTA staff hosted 13 on-street engagements at bus stops and transfer points throughout the Bronx and northern Manhattan to promote the survey. Nearly 10,000 brochures were distributed during the events and an additional 6,000 were distributed on buses. • Over 1,300 local and express bus surveys were completed between June and August 2019.
### [p168_c0003] Additional outreach:
- [p168_c0004] • The Plan was promoted across social channels and digital assets, including in subway stations and on buses • A press release was issued to announce the Draft Plan and Public Open Houses: http://www.mta.info/press-release/nyc-transit/mta-releases-draft-plan-redesign-bronx-bus-network • A presentation was given to the joint Bronx Borough Service Cabinet/Borough Board at Borough Hall: https://www.bronxnet.org/watch/videos/7560/

## Page 171

### [p171_c0001] Network Drawing Sessions & Bus Depot Sit-Downs: March 2019
[p171_c0002] As part of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign, we engaged with our Road Operations team, union leadership, and bus operators and dispatchers at each of the five bus depots in the Bronx.
[p171_c0003] Bus Planning works with Road Operations on a regular basis and we rely on them to provide us with insight from the road/field perspective on any routing, bus stop, or service frequency and span proposals. We also hold quarterly meetings with the unions to obtain feedback from them and inform them of upcoming projects.
[p171_c0004] In development of our Draft Plan, we held Network Drawing Sessions with road operations, unions, NYCDOT, government and community relations, bus scheduling, and bus planning staff. We held two sessions on March 14th and 15th that focused on regular bus service (Local, Limited, and Select Bus Service). The first session focused on identifying key corridors that would sustain all-day coverage (30 minutes or better), frequent (15 minutes or better), and very frequent (8 minutes or better) service. This was a very successful exercise and allowed all stakeholders to take ownership over the redesign. Several weeks later, a second drawing session was held in which bus planning staff shared very draft route proposals with the group. Each proposal was reviewed by the group with feedback shared to incorporate into the proposals. Following the end of the second drawing session, a link was circulated to all attendees providing a full draft Bronx Bus Network map in Remix, a bus service planning tool. Brainstorming session for express bus service was also held on May 8th with MTA bus planning, bus scheduling, road operations, unions, and NYCDOT staff. Similar to the earlier drawing sessions, routing options were discussed with all stakeholders agreeing on which route alignments would move forward for the redesigned express bus network.
[p171_c0005] In addition to the network drawing sessions, a team of MTA staff held Depot Sit-Downs where they spoke with and surveyed bus operators and dispatchers at each of the five Bronx bus depots. We received route-specific feedback and general challenges that they face as well as suggested solutions.
### [p171_c0006] Major challenges included:
- [p171_c0007] • Fare evasion • Customers not following bus guidelines, protocol, and procedures • Aggressive automobile drivers using the bus lane to pass the flow of traffic • Construction and pedestrians obstructing the flow of traffic • Taxis, Transportation Network Companies (TNCs), delivery trucks, and other vehicles parking or stopping in the bus lane or stop to load/unload • Pedestrians and cyclists posing safety concerns
### [p171_c0008] Recommended solutions included:
- [p171_c0009] • Address fare enforcement • Remove farebox from buses and require passengers to pay prior to boarding bus (like SBS) • Increase Eagle Team presence on the bus and at bus stops
[p171_c0010] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 171_

## Page 172

- [p172_c0001] • Improve communication • More signage and public announcements for customers regarding upcoming service changes and bus policies • Road Operations, dispatchers, and Bus Scheduling should meet and discuss changes with bus operators or ride the buses during peak periods to better inform scheduling changes • Line and service changes • Increase service on lines with high crowding • Increase the number of SBS routes • Reroute buses • 96th St instead of 116th St and 5th Av (BxM6, BxM7, BxM9, BxM10) • Avoid right turns on narrow streets • Bus lane and stop enforcement • Greater fines and citations for vehicles in violation of bus stop or lane • Increase number of bus lanes
[p172_c0002] The Bus Planning team then proceeded to refine route proposals, bus stop removals, and frequencies for certain routes that warranted an increase. These proposals made up the bulk of the Bronx Bus Network Redesign Draft Plan.

## Page 174

### [p174_c0001] Project Launch and Public Education: August 2018-January 2019
[p174_c0002] The Bronx Bus Network Redesign launched publicly on September 5, 2018. The public launch was preceded by several meetings with Bronx elected officials and other stakeholders.
[p174_c0003] Kick-off included a series of actions:
- [p174_c0004] • Introduction of the project microsite: https://new.mta.info/bronxbusredesign • A press release announcing the project and upcoming public workshops: http://www.mta.info/press-release/nyc-transit/mta-nyc-transit-announces-community-workshops-help-reshape-future-bronx • A presentation to a joint meeting of the Bronx Service Cabinet/Borough Board and a video is available at https://www.bronxnet.org/watch/videos/5745/
[p174_c0005] The initial series of public workshops was designed to introduce the goals of a bus network redesign to our customers and interested stakeholders. To promote the workshops, posters were distributed to all Bronx elected officials and community boards as well as on buses, in subway stations, and by request.
[p174_c0006] Six workshops were held at locations around the Bronx in September and October 2018.
[p174_c0007] Community Board 12 Thursday, September 20, 2018
[p174_c0008] Metropolitan College of New York Thursday, September 27, 2018
[p174_c0009] Monroe College - Kings Hall Wednesday, October 3, 2018
[p174_c0010] RiverBay Corporation Co-Op City Tuesday, October 9, 2018
[p174_c0011] NYC Health + Hospitals/Jacobi Monday, October 15, 2018
[p174_c0012] Christ Church Riverdale Thursday, October 18, 2018
[p174_c0013] MTA also conducted an intercept and online survey during this phase. Intercept surveys were conducted at 12 key locations and nearly 2,000 surveys were completed. Additionally, a parallel survey was available on our website and was promoted at the workshops and via community outreach and coordination with elected officials. Seven hundred fifty people completed the online version of this survey.
[p174_c0014] More information about these workshops and survey findings can be found in the Existing Conditions Report.
[p174_c0015] _The Bronx Bus Network Redesign: Final Plan | 174_
